CHICAGO GRAIN MARKET.
CHICAGO, May I?.â Claims of serious dam-
age by Hessian flies, light receipts and re-
ported drought ln Russia started wheat trad-
ers on the rampage at the opening. The pit
was flooded with buying orders by the bulls
and shorts were forced to cover. As a result
%c -was added to last, night's closing price
during the first half hour's trading. Profit tak-
ing on the bulge, however, checked the up-turn
and sent prices off a cent, but outside demand
took care of the liquidation and the rally frorm.
the break was as prompt as the decline had
been. : ' , . , ,
After that the market ruled quiet within
narrow limits until . the close. Reduced esti-
mates by' prominent statisticians of the winter
wheat yield encouraged - buying. July opened
a shade higher at 73%@74c, advanced to 74%
@74% c, declined to 73% c, and closed with buy-
ers at 73% c. -'; ' " ' V ' -
Corn ruled weak, Influenced by favorable
growing weather and Increase in the country
movement and slack cash demand. July closed
%c lower. ">'-.â â  â â  '1 . . "â â â¢â â¢
Oats â¢ declined under liquidation and short
selling due to favorable crop reports.
Extensive buying of lard by packing con-
cerns and higher prices for hogs strengthened
provisions. Pork advanced 7%c, lard ,7% _ 10c
and ribs . 5c. ;

LONDON WOOL SALES.
LONDON, May 19.â third series of the
wool auction sales closed to-day with the usual
good attendance.. The offerings numbered ' 7758
bates and included a fair selection of merinos
and especially scoured, which brought out
active competition. Greasy was actively
bought by . France and â  New Zealand cross-
breds were In large supply and were prin
cipally taken by Yorkshire at full rates. The
general . tone at the close of the sale to-day
was very firm. To-day's Continental advices
reported terminal markets again advanced 10
centimes. During the series ended to-day prac
ticably the whole available amount catalogued
was sold, only 4500 bales being carried .over. |
The Continental buyers purchased 95,000 bales
and the home buyers 85.000.

WHEAT AND OTHER GRAINS.
WHEATâ A good deal of lurid bull news Is |
being received here and at Chicago, but it has !
little effect on the market. Yesterday's Install- '
i ment reported a strong Chicago market, with j
! foreigners buying. The news from Russia was \
! unfavorable, and the crop outlook in the Dan- ]
I Ã¼blan and Black Sea districts was quoted as
sensationally bad. Snow, the statistician, an- !
j nounced that winter wheat had gone back fast :
' in the past ten days, and that the country i
would not raise 275.000.000 bushels. Toward the
close the Chicago market shaded off on heavy
sales of long wheat. '

THE STOCK MARKET.
Securities were not as active on the morning
session of the Bond Exchange. The feeling was
weak as a rule and Giant Powder declined to
$77 50 and Contra Costa Water to $69 8.%.
There were no marked changes on the after
noon call.
noon call. - . ' .
Mining stocks were rather better under the
usual quiet business. The telegram from the
pump said: "Second elevator is working stead-
ily The water is 177 feet below the 1750 level
and 203 feet below the Sutro tunnel discharge
boxes." .
The Consolidated California and Virginia as
sessment of 25c per share will be delinquent in
the boards to-day. t .
The annual meeting of the Seg. Belcher and
Mldes Consolidated Mining Company has been
called for June 6. _

declared an extra dividend of â¢$1 per share,

two" and will make $1,120,000 in dividends since
January L 1895.

a dividend of 40c per share to-day. __._

The report from the Standard Consolidated
mine at Bodle for the week ending May 13
states that raise 4, in the Moyle vein, 150 level,
shows 14 inches of fair ore in the top. Raise
2 In the New vein on the 318 level- has cut 48
inches of low-grade ore and has been stopped.
Raise 4 ln No. 10 vein on the 31S level has IS |
inches of fair ore in the top. The south drift i
ln the same vein on the 380 level has 12 Inches
of fair ore on the hanging wall side. In the
Bulwer east crosscut on the 528 level they are
cleaning out and laying a new track. The
stopes are yielding the usual quantity of fair
to good ore from various points on the 270,
318, 336. 470, 528 and 582 levels. At the mill 256
tons of ore were crushed during the week.
Average assay value vahner tailings, $13 48;
concentrates produced. IVi tons; assay value,
$1245 7S; plata amalgam produced, 879 troy
ounces; average assay value per ounce, $1 80.
Tailings plant No. 1 treated 253% tons of tail
ings for the week. Plant No. 2 treated 165
tons tailings.
New properties of the Standard Con. at Su-
gar Pine, Cal. (Excelsior mine): In the shaft, I
sinking was resumed May 13. Total -depth of
shaft, 219% feet. On the 211 level the station
timbers have been put in at the 211 level and
crosscut No. 1 has been advanced to a total
length of 17 feet. The old adit level has been
cleaned out for 14 feet.

SUN, MOON AND TIDE
United States Coast and Geodetic Survey-
Times and Heights of High and Low
Waters at Fort Point, entrance to San
Francisco Bay. Published by official au
thority of the Superintendent .
NOTEâ The high and low waters occur at
the city front (Mission-street wharf) about
twenty-five minutes later than at Fort Point;
the height of tide Is the same at both places.
NOTEâ In the above exposition of the tides
the early morning tides are given ln the left
hand column and the successive tides of the
day in the order of occurrence as to time. Th.
second time column gives the second tide of
the day, the third time column the third tide
and the last or right hand column gives the
last tide of the day. except when there are but
three tides, as sometimes occur. The heights
given are additions to the soundings on tho
United States Coast Survey charts, except
when a minus sign <â ) precedes the height.
and then the number given is subtracted from
the depth given by the charts. The plane of
reference is the mean of the lower low waters.

1: takes a mighty keen person to win
â¢:-.\ money at Oakland track these clos
ing up days. One possessed of a dark
lantern and a jimmy has the best
chance. The judges must have discarded
their fold glasses, else they don't know
rich* from wrong. Ames put up a gro
tesque ride on the favorite February in
the third event, but nothing was said.
The ring took all sorts of liberties with
the mare, hut the officials didn't know it;
didn't care probably. This was one inci
dent. A bad spill In the second race was
the other. At the far turn Sylvan I. ass.
Gilt Edge; Anchored and Solstice went
down In a heap. The riders all escaped
serious injury with the exception of "old
man" Steward, who was badly bruised.
Solstice hobbled off the track on three
loc.-;, hut the other nags ere unhurt.

Presiding Judge Graham Will Con-
Presiding Judge Graham Will Con-
sult Chief Lees as to the Advis-
ability of Trying More
Cases.
Fo- the second time a lurv In .Tndfre
Graham's court has brought In a verdict
of acquittal in the recent notorious poker
___>.-. .Ââ  iu_i v\;i.- mat of diaries W.
Redman, proprietor of the Palace saloon,
867 Market street, charged with permit
ting a -percentage game cf poker to be
played, and yesterday in the case of J.
H. Wilson, charged with conducting a
game in the same saloon, the jury within
ten minutes returned a verdict of acquit
tal. There is also the case of H. A. Hor-
Lein of the Cafe Royal, tried before a jury
in Judge Mogan's court, in which the
jury stood eleven for acquittal and one
for conviction. In view of these facts
Judge Graham says he will consult Chief
Lees to-day as to the advisability of go
ing to the trouble and expense of trying
any more cases of the kind.
When Wilson's case .was resumed yes
terday afternoon the cross-examination of
Policeman Tyrrell was concluded and Po
licemen G. XV. Meyer and John C. Mur
phy gave their testimony," which corrob
orated Eastman and Tyrrell's evidence.
This closed the case for the prosecution.
The defendant, Wilson, testified that no
more than two checks were taken from
each "pot" for a game and they were
utilized In providing the players with
liquor, cigars or sandwiches and for cards
and attendance. Redman, the proprietor,
and Samuel Aaron, the manager, testified
to the same effect. The average amount
taken from a table per hour was 51 36 and
as a rule the table was indebted to the
lloUSe. "3-^K*Â£l-5-9?-H_HB-!-9Â£VSâ^
After the testimony was all in the ques
tion of making an- argument to the jury
was discussed, and a juror put an end to
it by remarking: "We have heard enough
about it already." Both sides thereupon
waived an argument.
After being charged by the court the
jury retired and in ten minutes returned
a verdict of acquittal.

NEARLY SANK
TO HIS DEATH
IN SLIMY DOZE
Narrow Escape of F.
Blanchard.
â â¦ â
FELL IN A MUDDY SLOUGH
FELL IN A MUDDY SLOUGH
WENT DOWN UNTIL THE SLIME
REACHED HIS CHIN.
â â¦ â
Succor Ai river] Just as He Was Dis-
Succor Arrived Just as He Was Dis-
appearing Beneath the Black
Surface and Had Given
Up Hope.
+
ALAMEDA. May 19.â Frank Blanchard, j
a High street merchant, nearly met an
awful death last evening in the soft, !
slimy, black mud near the Bay Farm Is- â 
land bridge. He had sunk to his chin in'
the ooze and in .a moment more would
have disappeared beneath the mud. when ;
a couple of men. attracted by his cries for
help, appeared on the scene and rescued |
him.
- -hard, who Is a very heavy man,
was attempting to board a dredger In j
course of construction. it was some feet ;
from the shore of a muddy slough and |
the only means of getting aboard was by
crossing a plank. When Blanchard was
midway between the shore and the
dredger the plank broke under his weight,
dropping him feet first into the mud.
He attempted to make his way to shore
or at least where he could grasp one end
of the broken plank, but instead of mak
ing headway he only sank deeper and
deeper into the slime as he continued hie j
struggles. Finally the mud reached his
hips. No help was In sight and his re
peated calls for succor remained unan- I
swered. Darkness was rapidly coming |
and he felt himself being slowly drawn,
down by the suction of the mud.
The ooze finnllv reached his armpits.
Hestruggled to prolong his life by stretch
ing forth his arms to stay the downward
movement toward sure death, biij. his
arms found no support and they also were
soon beneath the mud. As the slime
crawled up toward his neck and the little
crabs began to play tag around him he
gave one desperate yell for help and was
rewarded by a reply. â ','.'
The searchers had heard his first calls
but failed to locate him. They were with
in twenty feet of the slough and were
about to turn back, thinking they were
the victim of a slier, when Blanchard's
last shriek attracted them.
The broken plank was thrown to j
Blaiichard and while he clung to it and
kept himself above the surface the men
secured a rope, and finally with additional j
assistance pulled the victim out of the
slough and from the verge of a muddy
grave.
BLIND JOSEPH
SANDERS WILL
TAKE CONTROL
H Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
908 Broadway, May 19.
After experiencing four years of a grad
ual decline in the manufacture of broom Â»
and the Incomes of its inmates, the Home
for Adult Blind will have a new superin
tendent June 1. This step has been de
cided upon by the new board of directors
appointed by Governor lags.
The. nation of Superintendent. Hays
has been accepted, and the blind superin
tendent, Joseph Sanders, who was de
posed four years ago by a Democratic
administration, after a long term of suc
cessful management, will be reinstated.
Superintendent Sanders is one of the
Meverest blind, men of the age, and the
manner in which he conducted the Blind
Home was such that a great number of
visitors of the Institution could not be
persuaded that he was without his sight.
The new board consists of Colonel John
P. Iris:: and Directors Spaulding, Sanborn,
Wells and Randolph, and they are unani
mous in making the change. For many
years the Blind Home has practically
failed of its purpose, and for a consider
able time the broom factory, its solo
source of revenue outside the State appro
priation, has been closed. This step was
taken by order of the directors, who dis
covered that under existing conditions
they were making brooms at a loss and
could not dispose of them when they
were made. The only means by which the
blind men could procure pocket money
and funds with which to buy clothes was
by making brooms, and last winter many
of them suffered fearfully from the cold
weather for want of proper clothing. It
has always been the contention of old
members of the board of directors that
with a practical blind superintendent with
a thorough knowledge of tie- broom corn
market the home could be maintained
ln such a manner as to produce a fair
income. Such an Income was produced
all the time Superintendent Sanders was
in office.
Secretary Havens has also been de
posed and George S. Meredith of the old
Republican City Central Committee has
been appointed secretary. The regular
meeting of the board will be held June l.
at which time the new superintendent
will take office, and it is probable that the
patronage of the Institution will see other
changes.
Last evening the retiring superintend
ent. John Hays, was presented with a
gold watch by the employee of the Insti
tution. The Informal affair took place at
lilt- home and was marked by words of
appreciation on both sides.
INSPECTOR ERWIN
RETURNS FROM CUBA
He Bring- Some Interesting Informa
tion Regarding the Attitude of
tion Heg-arding the Attitude of
Natives Toward Us.
Natives Toward Us.
â¢ BRKELET. Ma. 19. Postofflce In-'
BERKELEY. May 19.â Postoffice In-*
spector J. W. Erwin returned to-night
from Cuba, where has has been engaged
under General E. (Â». Rathbone in organ
izing the United States mail service for
.he island. He left for California on the
22d of last month, staying two weeks in
Washington. D. C.
Mr. Erwin brings word that the con
dition of things In the island is very
quiet. He was favorably impressed with
the Cubans and thinks them well dis
posed toward the United States. It is his
opinion that if 'a vote were take,, of the
native population It would be largely in
.favor of annexation. Opposition, he ex
plained, was due to certain political agi
tators, but the influence of these was fast
waning. The war, he said, had left the
Interior of the country In a most dep.or
abie state, and a certain kind of fever,
termed \by the natives "Weyler fever,"
was spreading everywhere.
In certain parts or the Island the crops
for this season were a failure. With re
gard to the mail service, Mr. Erwin ex
plained that It bad been reorganized
tipon the American system and was now
In thorough working order under charge
of General Rathbone. â

The Market Street and Eureka Valley
Improvement Club recently held a very
busy meeting. Reports were received from
the committees on transfers at junction
cf Market and Church streets, on by-laws
and on loinlng the Federation of Mission
Clubs. The petition to Supervisors for

Seventeenth to Valencia was signed. A
resolution was passed backing up the â 
Mayor in his efforts to maintain the Jl-10
rate for gas; and recommending members
to refuse to pay any more than _ that
amount. The scheme presented by 1 resi
dent Cuthbertson of a park panhandle
from junction of Market and Dolores to
the entrance of the present panhandle
was adopted, the matter to be laid befÂ°re
the Merchants' Association and th- im
provement clubs throughout the city
Meeting nights were changed to - ruiays.

"FIGHTING SIXTH" ARRIVES
Vanguard Came Yesterday En Route j
for the Philippines.
The vanguard of the Sixth United
States Infantry, known as the "Fighting
Sixth," arrived in this city yesterday.
Company A, 'with 112 men, came over on
the 8 o'clock boat and were escorted to
the transport Sherman at the foot of
Folsom street wharf by Captain Noble of
General Shatter's staff, where they inline- ;
dlatelv embarked. They expressed much
satisfaction at the reception they re
ceived and were the objects of much
kindly Interest by passengers on the Terry
boat. The remaining companies of the I
regiment will reach San Francisco to- |
morrow. ;""i .
Each of the men has a complete equip
ment for service in the tropics, one year s ;
supply of clothing and 100 rounds of am
munition. The train on which they came
was made up of fourteen cars and ex
perienced no mishaps. The officers occu- ,
pied a Pullman and the men were in three i
tourist sleepers. Eight cars carried the j
regimental baggage and eight days' ra
tions for each man. Colonel kollogg, who
is in command of the regiment, will ar
rive on Sunday.
MEDICOS TO DEDICATE
THEIR NEW BUILDING
COLLEGE OF PHYSICIANS WILL
LAY CORNERSTONE.
Ceremonies Will Be Conducted Under
the Auspices of Grand Lodge
of Free Masons.
At noon to-day the -College of
Physicians and Surgeons will dedi
cate their new building in course of erec
tion on Fourteenth street, between Va
lencia and Mission. The ceremonies will
consist of the laying of a cornerstone and
literary exercises.
The new building Is a large, square.
three-storied structure, the first story of
which is already finished. It will be sev
eral months before the college will house
its students in the new quarters.
The programme of literary exercises,
which lias been arranged by Dr. Alfred
E. Regensburger, Thomas Morffew and
Winslow Anderson, the committee of ar
rangements, will be under the direction
of Professor J. R.;Lalne, president of the
college. The cornerstone will be laid un
der the auspices of the Grand Lodge of
Free and Accepted Masons of the State
of California. Judge F. M. Angellotti.
grand master, performing the ceremo
nies. The Masonic quartet will furnish
the vocal music of the exercises. Mayor
Phelan will deliver an address, after
which the quartet will sing "The Star
Spangled Banner." Judge K. B. Carpen
ter will deliver an address, followed by
a selection by Cassasa's band. The last
aidless will be that of Congressman Ju
lius Kahn.
Every preparation is being made to ac
commodate a large crowd.
GREAT RICHES AT CAPE NOME
Private Letters Frirm Unalaklik Con-
firm the News oi a Great Strike.
Private letters that are now arriving
from the gold fields confirm t he news of
a rich rind at Cape Nome. One dated at
"Unalaklik, January 7, 189.," says there
are "bigger and richer gold fields there
than anything the Klondike can show."
There are acres and acres of rich claims,
and the men now on the ground chnnot
begin to locate them all. No labor can
be had for love or money, and it is a case
of every man for himself. Says â¢ the
writer: "The Cape Nome fields are going
to stir up things more than the Klondike
discoveries did. They pay from the sur
face down and Is only five feet to bed
rock." -"v'Y:
COCHRAN WILL AGAIN
COACH BERKELEY
Garrett Cochran, the Famous Princeton End.
BERKELEY, May 19.â Garrett Cochran, the. famous Princeton end, will
coach the University of California football team through the coming
season. This news came in a dispatch â  received to-night from Silver
City. New Mexico. 'â ' Â',.,"V ; : ".-.;; . .
Cochran's remarkably successful work with the Berkeley men last year
has made him the idol of all the U. C. students, and the news that he will
once again train the blue and gold for Its annual contest with the cardinal
will be received with the greatest satisfaction by all Berkeley collegians.
While the dale of his return to California is not yet-known. It will doubt
less-be very soon after the opening of the next college term. As -the time
set for this is August 14 the big coach will in all probability be here not later
than the beginning of September. ._â  ,* ''."'",', > \ .- '.
Cochran's services for a second season have only been secured after the
greatest -difficulty on the part of the university athletic association. After
laj_. Thanksgiving he decided to forsake the gridiron altogether, and he left
Berkeley with' the understanding that he should fmd a substitute in another
Princeton man. But Football Manager Irwin J. ' Muma has made repeated ef
forts to induce Cochran to change his mind, and as a last resort he took the
trip to Silver City. New Mexico, in the . hope of concluding some arrange
ments. That he has been . successful is shown by the telegram which brings
the news. '. ':.'-... . ..._.-. -:.-â '.-..., . v__.
Fortunately/ for the blue and gold the personnel of next year's team will
differ but slightly from the victorious eleven of last season. Percy Hall will
return to college; next August, and with him will "be Griesberg. ; Kaarsburg,
Athearn, Bart Thane, "Whipple, Hooper, Smith and Womble. Masters, will
probably succeed Craig as end; his good work In Portland .-"."â¢last Christmas
shows; him to be full of promise.' All the men have "the fullest confidence in
their ; coach, and the play they will put up may even exceed the good show
ing of last season. â¢â  â¢ "V - ;:;;' '^\ :';l ' '"'-.' â

How Isabella Turnbull Laing Openly
How Isabella Turnbull Laing Openly
Evinced Her AfEection for Rob-
crt Hill, Who Is Named
as Co-Respondent.
Oakland Office San Francisco Call,
908 Broadway, May 19.
Flirting at their wooden wedding last
January Is made the basis of a most, sen- '
sational cross-complaint and answer filed j
late this afternoon by Peter Miller Laing, !
, whose wife, Isabella Turnbull Lalng, is |
; suing for a divorce on the ground of ex
. treme cruelty. ;
| The defendant husband alleges: "That
on January 7, 1899. while they were cele-
I brating the anniversary of their wooden
j wedding, Isabella T. Laing. in the pres
j ence of all the guests, openly and wan
! tonly flirted with Robert Hill, a single
man, and thereafter almost daily up to
March 31 left her home to visit at the
| home of Robert Hill, for whom she no-
toriously evinced**\her affection, cruelly
: neglecting defendant and failing on nu
merous occasions to cook his meals."
Robert Hill is named as co-respondent,
and throughout the cross-complaint many
I clandestine meetings between the wife
and Hill, both here and at her sister's
home in Alameda and at the home of a
Mr. Hunter, are cited as damaging cir
cumstances of her infidelity.
"On numerous occasions," continues the
plaintive and alleged wronged husband, i
"Hill was seen to hug and kiss Isabella
Laing, and on one occasion â¢ defendant
asked her not to have- anything more to
do with said Hill, but she answered: 'I ;
would not do anything to harm that
boy." " All of which caused Mr. Lalng
, much mental anguish. \
Complaining further. Laing charges ,
, his wife with intemperance, cruelty and :
conspiracy. The latter consists of an al- ;
leged scheme hatched between Mrs.
Laing and her brother John, whereby a i
sister Jamirria was brought to the Laing
! home one evening to cook Laing's sup
; per and remain there all night, while Mrs.
Lalng stayed at the home of her brother.
"Hut." explains the cross-complaint, "di-
vining the purpose of . his wife, he sent
Jamima to her room ln Oakland."
The allegations of cruelty and Improper
relations with this sister made in Mrs.
j Laing's complaint are all severally denied '
I by the defendant, though he admits that !
I oh four occasions he took Jamima buggy-
I riding at the request of plaintiff: and the
charge by the wife that defendant com-
pelled or ordered her to go to Madame
: Jaequez to have a criminal operation per-
formed is also denied and answered by
i cross-complaining that Mrs. Lalng went
to Madame Jacques voluntarily on the:
i advice of a lady friend.
These and divers other actions, Laing .
asserts, caused him great shame and
scandal and inflicted upon him grievous
mental anguish, degrading and humiliat- I
ing him in the eyes of the world, where
; fore he asks for a decree dissolving to the
I bonds of matrimony and assigning to the
i respective parties their share of the com
munity property, which consists of a
house and lot on Blame avenue, near
Twelfth street, and 'about $600 worth of
personal property. ' j
WIGNEY'S BODY FOUND.
He Fell From the Olympic Pier Near
the Cliff House a Month Ago.
The mutilated body of George A. Wig
ney was discovered yesterday morning in
a rocky cove near the suction pipe of the
Sutro Baths by H. B. Nabb. The : head
and both hands were gone and the re
mains were, very much decomposed.
Wigney was 20 years old and a clerk by
occupation.: On April 14 of this year he
paid a visit to the Cliff House beach with
his mother 'sister. He went to the
end of the Olympic Club pier, a very dan
gerous place, and while reading a book
fell or jumped off into the water. The
body was not recovered until yesterday.
The body was taken to the Morgue and
was identified there by the mother and
two sisters of the deceased, the identifica
tion having been made possible by the
laundry marks on the underclothing. The
lamentations of the grief-stricken women
were most distressing.
The remains were turned over by. Coro
ner Hill to an Alameda undertaker, and
the funeral will be held from the family
residence, 1562 Railroad avenue, Alameda,
Russ Family Will Race.
The male members of the Russ family,
well-known in this city. Will hold a road
race among themselves to-morrow over
the San Carlos five-mile course. Each
participant is a member of the family,
either directly or by marriage. The en
tries and handicaps are as follows:
E. F. Russ, scratch; 11. S. Russ and Joe
Ahearn. one and a half minutes; Rus
RuÂ«s, two minutes; F. G. Wegener, two
and a half minutes; R. R. Russ. three
minutes; Ed Boedefeld, four minutes;
Fred Russ, six and a half minutes; W. B.
Wegener, seven minutes. The three who<
reach the tape last will buy a dinner for
the others. E. F. Russ, the scratch man,
Is the Olympic courier who helped win
the relay race last Sunday. â 
Last Chance to See the Pope.
The grand benefit for St. Rose's Church
will be given this evening at Metro
politan Temple under the auspices of the
Young Ladies' Sodality of the parish. The
biograph pictures of Pope' Leo XIII will
be a leading feature in addition to a pro
gramme of unusual merit. This will be
the last opportunity for the public to view
the moving pictures of the Pope.
Recitations will be given by XV. Walsh
and T. J. Hickey; musical numbers con
tributed by Misses Kilgariff and Stanley
and Messrs. Desmond, Lane, Vargas,
Ruff and Lorringer; comic selections by
Messrs. Hynes, Sheerin, Gleason and Mc-
Mahon. The proceeds of the affair will
Â§o to the maintenance of St. Rose's
chool.
Alex Loughborough's Pastime.
Last evening Alexander Loughborough,
who shot "Buck" Morse in this city some
i time ago, and "Blockers" Hanley enter
j tamed a party of friends in a side room
j of the Grotto, opposite the City Hall.
i An overindulgence in beer caused a mv
' tual disagreement, during which some of
: the party amused themselves by throwing
] bottles and glasses at an inoffensive
waiter. .v.;:*.-
Officer Butterworth was called, and, in
company with Coroner Hill, who hap
: pened to be in the resort, quelled the dis
i turbance. In the meantime a riot alarm
was sent to the Central station and a
number of officers were dispatched to the
scene. No arrests' were made.
Police Cannot Have the Tug.
The matter of giving the quarantine tug
used by the Board of Health to the Po
lice Department for use along the water
front came up for consideration before
the Health and Police Committee of the
Board of Supervisors yesterday. After
some discussion it was decided that fur
ther consideration of the, matter be In
definitely postponed, which means that
the police will not get the boat.
The National Athletic Club was granted
8 permit to conduct a boxing contest on
some date between the, Ist and the H'Jih of
next month.'
Makes Her Life Miserable.
John J. Coffey, a teamster, was con
victed by Judge Mogan yesterday on the
charge of battery upon Mary Paul, a tail
oress who works at 62 Tehama street. The
girl testified that she at one time kept
company with Coffey, but gave him up.
Since then he has made her life miserable
by following her everywhere and spring
ing out of doorways upon her and fright
ening her. May 17 be grabbed her as she
was leaving her work, and struck her.
Coffey will get a severe sentence .to-day.

In the Divorce Court.
Superior Judge Daingerlield granted
Maria F. Dutra a divorce from Jose Du
tra yesterday on the ground of cruelty.
Suits for divorce have been filed by Wil
liam Short against Mary B. Short for in
temperance, Emma Meigs against J. J.
Meigs on the ground that the defendant
was convicted of a felony, and Thomas
I 'rid. more against Margaret on the
ground of desertion.
To Be Made a Test Case.
E. A. Fisher of the Oberon appeared In
acting Police Judge Groezinger's court
yesterday to answer a charge of conduct
ing a theater without paying the proper
license. As several other places are in
the same position It was intimated that
the case would be made a test one and it
was continued till Monday. ;.;:~

THE OHIO'S FIRST RIVET.
Work on the Nation's Defender Com-
menced at- the Union Iron Works.
.The work of .building the hull of the
Ohio was commenced at the Union Iron
Works yesterday. . During the past few
weeks men have been . busy shaping the
ribs j and plates, and, having got all the
pieces in place for the start, it was or
dered yesterday that the first rivet' shout
be driven into place in trie keel -of the
great naval fighter. There was- no un
usual ceremony in the driving of this first
rivet, except that a greater number than
usual of the officers of the. yard were on
hand. , .
Besides the building of this huge man
of-war the Union Iron Works has four
other vessels on the ways. The construc
tion of these has taxed every inch of
available space in the shipyard and at
the same time has been .the means of giv
ing work to about 3000 men.

of the stockholders of the Olympic Salt Water

NOTICE Is hereby given by order of the Board
of Directors of the OCEANIC STEAMSHIP
COMPANY that a meeting of the stockholders
of said Company has been called by said
Board, to be held on FRIDAY, the second day
of June, A. D. 1899, at 11 o'clock in the fore-
noon of said day, at the principal place of
business of said Company, at the building
where the said Board of Directors usually
meets, namely, at the oflfce of said Company.
number 327 Market St., In the City and County
of San Francisco, State of California; that
the object of said meeting is to consider and
act upon the proposition that said Company
create a bonded Indebtedness of two million
five hundred thousand dollars ($2,500,000). In
United States gold coin, for the- purpose of
raising money to complete the construction
of Its steamships and their equipment, for
use in the business of this corporation, and
to purchase and pay for any other property
within the purposes of this Comi_-ny; and to
secure the bonded Indebtedness so proposed
. to be created by a mortgage upon Its steam
and sailing shins and all other property of
said Company now owned or hereafter to be
i acquired by said Company.
By order of the Board of Directors of the
Oceanic Steamship Company.
[Corporate Seal.] E. H. SHELDON.
Secretary of the Oceanic Steam-hip Com-
pany. â â  '

BOLD DEFENSE
OF ORGANIZED
LABOR UNIONS
Sentiment of S. F.
Labor Council.
â â¦ â
DENOUNCES GEN. MERRIAM
DENOUNCES GEN. MERRIAM
UTTERANCES OF IDAHO'S GOV-
ERNOR CRITICIZED.
â¢
A Very Strong Resolution Defining
A Very Strong Resolution Defining
the Position of the Laboring
Man to Be Sent to Presi-
dent McKinley.
At a meeting of the San Francisco La
bor Council last evening the action of the
military authorities in dealing with the
strikers at Wardner. Idaho, and the sen
timents of Major General Merriam and
Governor Steunenberg regarding labor or
ganizations were denounced in a caustic
resolution, a copy of which will be for
warded to the President of the United
States that he may feel the pulse of San
Francisco toilers on the Wardner situa
tion.
The resolution was drafted by a com
mittee appointed at a previous meeting
and adopted last night with but a sin
gle dissenting voice. Its purport Is a con
tradiction of the expression of Idaho's
Governor that labor organizations are
criminal in purpose and prohibitive .of
employment to members thereof; also
that |the utterances of Major General
Merriam are the underminings of civil
liberty. it is as follows:
Whereas, a condition of momentous gravity
has risen from the conduct .-i the State and
Federal authorities in dealing with the parties
suspected of comDllclty In the destruction of
th- Hunker Hill and Sullivan mill at Wtird
ner Idaho, on April 29. 1599; and
Whereas, this condition is the result of ut
terances made by Major General Merriam, I*.
S. A., while in authority on the scene, to the
effect that trade unions should be legally pro
hibited as criminal conspiracies, followed by a
proclamation of Governor Steunenberg of
Idaho, which declares that "certain organiza
tions or combinations (the miners' unions) ex
isting in Shoshone County have shown them
selves to he criminal in purpose by destroying
property and permitting murder." and pro
hibiting the employment by mine-owners of
men -'belonging to said or other criminal or
ganizations" during the continuance of mar
tial law, with the alternative of closing the
mines; therefore be It
Resolved, by the San Francisco Labor Coun
cil, that we condemn the language of Major
General Merriam as a malicious attack upon
organized labor an.l a threat against all forms
of civil liberty; and further
Resolved, That we condemn the action of
Governor Steunenberg in declaring the cer
tain organizations or combinations in ques
tionâ to wit. the miners' unionsâ to be crim
inal In purpose, and prohibiting: the employ
ment of members thereof, as -an assumption
opposed to the known facts,- an arrogant
stretch of authority under martial law, and
a total subversion of the principle, underlying
the determination of both law' and equity, that
trial and conviction must precede condemna
tion and punishment; and further
Resolved. That we urgently protest against
the cruel and Inhuman treatment of the min
ers nd others now under arrest at Wardner,
end against the arrest and removal of the civil
officers of Shoshone County and appointment of
others chosen with a view to their pliancy
under the military regime, as an, aggravation
el the main indictments, designed for the pur
pose of terrorizing the community and the
public at large; and further
Resolved. That we see in the present situa
tion at Wardner. Idaho, a definite relation to
the recently inaugurated policy of the Govern
ment, which repudiates the principle of equal
and Inalienable rights, as applied to those peo
ples of other countries with whom the Govern
ment Is now at war, and, therefore, that this
situation clearly forecasts the extension of
that policy with the same results to all the
people of the United States; and further
Resolved. That we submit this statement of
our position to th* public In the hope and con
fidence that It will arouse the fullest sense of
the danger involved in these conditions. We
deplore the acts of violence against property
and the deaths that have occurred in the af
fected locality, but we deny that the.. cir
cumstances afford any justification for the
course now being pursued by the authorities.
The civil authorities are vested with full
power to punish the persons responsible for
these crimes, and- we pledge our assistance to
that end by .-very means compatible with law.
We. therefore, declare that the action of Gen
eral Merriam and Governor **teunenberg is
conclusive evidence of a policy to destroy civil
government and to establish upon the ruins
thereof an oligarchs dependent upon and sup
ported by military power. Confronted by this
condition. It behooves â¢ every citizen to voice

Ik founded, to reaffirm his allegiance to these

Peter Releus presented credentials from
the Milkers' Union and was given a place
in the council. The Sailors' Union re
ported that but 130 per month was paid
to seamen on Government transports and
that this is the smallest scale of wages
paid on any vessels. Certain contractors
who require men to ,york ten hours a day

the-next meeting of the council.
ANOTHER FOWLER
WILL DISCOVERED
FILED FOR PROBATE BY THE
DEVISEE'S ATTORNEY.
J? second will, purporting to have been
drawn by the late D. D. Fowler, the min
ing man,- who died at St. Luke's Hospital
on March 9 last, was filed for probate yes
terday. A few days after Fowler's death
a will was filed and admitted to probate
that bore date preceding his death but
five days. He left all bis property to his
children in this will with the exception
of $2500, which he bequeathed to Mrs. Wil
liam D. Fairer, of this city, who cared for
him during his last illness. Yesterday
another will, bearing date of October _._>,
IS9B, was tiled by Eugene Deuprey. This
will is witnessed by Thomas XV. Bethel.
603 Fell street, and Edwin C. Van Dyke,
at that time residing at St. Luke's Hos
pital, and with the exception that it dors
not mention Mrs. Farren is similar to the
first will filed. It reads:
Know all .men by these presents: That by
reason of th.- conduct of Ellie F. Fowler, in her
efforts to humiliate me and her apparent dis
regard of all wifely affection for me I do here
by revoke all wills and any will made by me
before the date hereof and particularly one
mede in her favor. ! further hereby declare
and will that my estate of whatsoever char
acter and wherever situate be distributed two
thirds therof to my Invalid child. Lizzie M.
Fowler, at St. .1...-. Mo., at Invalid Home, and
one-third thereof to Nellie I). Bennett, Bevier,
Mo. ; Frank B. Fowler. Kansas City, Kans..
and D. D. Fowler of th.- same place, share and
share alike, and I hereby appoint Thomas Kyle
and Thomas W. Bethel executors of this will.
In witness whereof 1 have Signed my name
to this, my last testament, consisting of one
and a third pages. D. I>. FOWLER.
Notwithstanding the fact that the first
will has been admitted to probate for a
purpose and a compromise effected be
tween decedent's will and the. devisees.
Mr. Deuprey went before Judge Coffey and
offered the will. Judge Coffey closely ex
amined the will and then asked the at
torney to what use he intended to put
the document, as 11. bore an â¢ earlier date
than the one already admitted. "The will
1 now present," answered Mr. Deuprey,
"although bearing an earlier date than
the one admitted, is of later execution
than the lirst and this we will prove." As
the date already admitted simply bears
decedent's X mark it Is quite probable
that a winning fight may be made on that
presented yesterday.
Evelyn Holt Was Absent.
Evelyn Holt, the woman who on Sep
tember 5 last tried to kill Conrad Pecker
with a pistol because the latter had mar
ried the Nemesis of Colonel Sutherland,
Mrs. Webber, did not appear when her
case was called for trial by Judge Lawlor
yesterday morning. A bench warrant
was in consequence issued by Judge Law
lor. fixing the defendant's bail at $2000,
hut it is doubtful that the warrant will
ever be served. It is said that Miss ii.it
has gone East to avoid trial and. is min
gled with the vast throngs of some big
Atlantic city when- it will be practically
impossible to detect her.

THE SAN FRANCISCO CALL, SATURDAY, MAY 20, 1899.
ATTACKED HER
LOVER WITH A
HORSEWHIP
Exciting Episode on
O'Farrell Street.
â * â
REVENGEFUL' WOMAN'S ACT
REVENGEFUL WOMAN'S ACT
â â¢â¦ â
MRS. DR. CLARK ASSAULTS
CHARLES LENAHAN.
Â»-
Jealous of His Attention to Cato de
Jealous of His Attention to Cato de
Hoop, She Waylays Them and
Uses Her Whip With ' .
Telling Effect. .
"You're a dirty cur; you profess to love
me and now I find you with another wo
man. Take that, you ingrate. and
that"-*â
"Thus spoke, Mrs. Dr. Frances Clark as
she applied a horsewhip, which she had
concealed under her sealskin coat, on the
head and shoulders of Charles Lenahan,
a well-known man about town and pro
fessional pianist.
The incident happened on O'Farrell
street near Stockton.
Lenahan, accompanied by another wo
man who is known as Cato de Hoop.
drove up to a saloon, intending to have
a bottle of wine, as Lenahan claims.
Scarcely hail they alighted from the
buggy when Mrs. Clark appeared "ii the
scene. After catching a glimpse <>l her
rival, whom she at once recognised, she
proceeded to upbraid Lenahan for his
conduct. The latter attempted to explain
that he had met the woman by accident.
when Mrs. Clark drew forth a whip
which sit.- had concealed in the folds of
her sealskin sacque and brought it down
on her lover's head. With a cry of pain
Lenahan started to join his companion,
who was seated In the buggy, but was
1 stopped by the infuriated woman. Ex-
citedly approaching her rival, Mrs. Clark
proceeded to belabor her with the whip.
"You're no woman," she indignantly re-
marked as she rained blow after blow on
the head and face of the astonished fe-
male. "I want you to understand that I
am engaged to marry this man" (point-
ing to Lenahan).- . .
"t The latter, after recovering from the
: suddenness of the attack, quickly seized
the whip and thus prevented Mrs. Clark
i from further injuring her rival. .
.With blood streaming down her face
Miss de Hoop jumped from the buggy
and assisted by a male friend 'who wit-
nessed the occurrence hastily left the
! scene.
Evidently maddened by her escape, Mrs.
, Clark, with the aid of her whip, proceed-
ed to be revenged on Lenahan. She at-
tacked him with tin- ferocity of a mad
I woman and amid declarations of unfaith-
fulness she repeatedly struck him over
- the head and shoulders with the whip.
A large crowd had collected by this time
anil they cheered the woman on.
i Satisfied that he was "up against It,"
as he expressed it. -Lenahan jumped into
his buggy and rapidly -drove away from
the scene. â ; . -
With a triumphant cry Mrs. Clark, re-
placed tho whip under her saccule and
disappeared down O'Farrell street.
. It is said that Mrs. Ciark is madly in-'
fatuated with Lenahan. Several days be-
fore the horsewhipping episode, it is au
thoritatively said that she wanted him
to marry her. It was aereed that they
i were to be married by a Justice of the
j Peace in Oakland, but she insisted that
the ceremony should be kept a secret.
According to Lenahan, she bought him a
magnificent diamond ring; in return he
purchased a marriage ring, which he gave
to Mrs. Clark. It was arranged that they
should meet at the Oakland ferry, pre-
paratory to crossing the bay and becom-
ing husband and wife, but at the last mm
ute Lenahan got "cold feet" and did not
materialize: Although angered' beyond
measure, Mrs. (.lark promised to forgive
him, provided he consented to marry her
in the near future.
W-ien,seen last night Lenahan admitted
that he had been horsewhipped by Mrs.
Clark, but persistently refused to giv*
any particulars.-
"It was only a love affair." he ex-
plained. "I got the worst of it and am
satisfied. See Mrs. Clark; she might tell
you what happened." /*"
Mrs. Clark, evidently determined not to
be Interviewed, has purposely kept out of
the way of reporters. Inquiry at her
home last night was met with the re-
sponse that she had left the .city, but
would return in a few days.
Miss de Hoop, who with Lenahan was
assaulted by Mrs. Clark, also refused to
talk about the occurrence.
"Pleas, don't say anything about it."
she pleaded last evening. "I was Indis
creet and got the worst of- it. I did not
know that Charley was engaged to marry
Mrs. Clark or I would not have gone for
a drive with him." *
Lenahan fears* that Mrs. Clark will su*
him for breach of promise of marriage,
but he claims be is prepared for any
emergency that might arise from his en
tanglement with her.

fied success. The Order was started about
a year ago in Seattle and has 6300 mem
bers. The local branch has a membership
of 500 and has only been in existence

BASEBALL TO-DAY.
Oakland and San Francisco to Fight
for the Lead.
A. grand contest for first plitce honors is
the card that" the California Baseball
League .offers to the cranks this week.
The Oakland dudes have fought their way
up near the top just In time to meet their
rivals on this side of the bay in 'a strug
gle for the leadership. : ' .
Manager Harris has been sneering at
the Oaklands of late and advising Cal
Ewing to go and hire a few -men who
could play ball, but when the dudes tool
three straight games from Watsonville
by some exceptionally line, ball playing
and settled down in second place the San
Francisco magnate began to take a seri
ous view of the situation. If he succeeds
in holding the lead after the coming en
gagement with the Oaklands he may con
sider himself very fortunate. The Oak
land team is now as good a fielding club
as there Is in the league, and it remains
to be seen whether the dudes can wield
the stick with sufficient effectiveness to
overcome the winning ways of the men
in black and gold.
The cranks on both sides of the bay
are looking forward to the coming con
tests with more than usual Interest, and
there will probably be more flamboyant
rooting at Recreation Park this week
than â¢ has developed since the opening of
the season.

BALDWIN ANNEX CAFE.
A New Restaurant and Billiard Hall
Opens Its Doors to the Public
;C: i To-Day.
For many weeks the Baldwin Annex,
.24-926-928 Market street and 25 Ellis street,
has been undergoing repairs in prepara
tion for the establishment of a cafe and
billiard hall that is second to. none in size
and elegance west of the Rocky Moun
tains. Its proprietorsâ Mr. G. Schmitt,
formerly proprietor of the "Fountain,"
for many years at the corner of Kearny
and Sutter streets, and Mr. J. XV. Orn
dorff. who was the first proprietor of the
Baldwin Hotel bar and billiard room
are favorably, known, not alone in this
city but throughout the coast, and are
thoroughly experienced caterers.
Under the personal direction of . Mr.
Schmitt, whose ideas have been closely
followed, the well-known firm of Haven
& Hopkins, architects, have produced an
effect in design and decoration that could
with difficulty be surpassed.
The main entrance on Market street,
twenty-one feet wide, is both imposing
and rich being finished in mahogany and
art glass. In, the Market-street front is
the billiard and bar room, to the purposes
of which tne large area is equally divided;
with Walnut-framed French plate mirrors
upon the one side and the handsome glass
finished bar extending the length of the
room on the other.
All kinds of refreshments will be served
and the cafe will be in charge of Mr.
Etonev ' Eragorri, the well-known chef.
Mr. John Fey, long associated with Mr.
Schmitt at the "Fountain," will be cash
ier. A mercantile lunch will be servea
from 11 a. m. to 2 p. m. Only the purest
wines and liquors will be kept in stock.
Imported Pilsener, Culmhacher, Eastern
and the popular brands of domestic beers
will be kept on draught.
One of th.- leading features of the Bald
win Annex Cafe is its billiard-room,
containing ten new tables of the latest
design of the Brunswick-Balke Company.
Two of these are sxlo and are the only
tables of thel size on the coast.
The following well-known contractors
have furnished the fittings and supplies:
Thomas Day & Co., chandeliers; (-has.
Brown & Sons, hardware; Swift & Co.,
lumber; Leo Aron, painter and decorator;
.- Boiler, tables; W. & J. Sloan.-, carpets
and draperies; West Coast Furniture
Company, woodwork; Duffy Bros., plumb
ing- XV. W. Montague & Co., ranges, etc.;
California Art Glass Company, art glass;
Rosencranz Company, electrical fixtures
and supplies. [-.
A DISUNIONIZED UNION.
The Mission Milkers Carrying the
White War Into the Police
court.
There is war, a white war, among the
Swiss milkers out on the Mission road.
That little social dance that was given
at the Six-mile House on last Saturday
night and which ended so disastrously
to the few who tried to adjust matters
between the union milkers and the can
cleaners has not subsided. The fight that
was precipitated in the dance hall and
which terminated with the demolition of
the front of the saloon in which tin; social
festivities were held was only the com
mencement of the lacteal war.
Since that unfortunate night fights,
which are termed "scraps" by Sergeant
Griffiths of the Seventeenth street police
station, have been the order of the day
and the night for that matter. In order
to save the Coroner a trip over College
Hill Captain Gillln has stationed three of
his athletic men on duty at the Six-mile
House. However, even the. presence of
these short-rib punchers have not been
sufficient to' quell the extractors of lacteal
fluid and can cleaners. The war has now
settled down between Joseph Regli and
Martin Schorne. The former had the lat
ter arrested a few days ago for battering
him on the, head with an empty milk
can. I The cuts were drawn together by
the surgeon's needle at the City and
County Hospital. Schorne, not to be out
done In the dispensation of justice as ad
ministered in the Police Courts, swore out
a warrant for the. arrest of Regli on the
charge of having made a vow that he
would give the. undertaker a job as soon
as the opportunity presented itself.
With this warrant Officer J. Dennan in
vaded the sacred precincts of Fassler's
dairy and in the name of the people of
the great State of California yanked
Hie 11 to prison. Judge Graham, however,
fixed his bond at $500. Whether his Honor
only valued Schorne's life at "these fig
ures or not the bond is silent.
A â  rehearsal of the "Disunionized
Union" will be had when the case is up
for hearing in the court. In the mean
time the milkers and the can cleaners
don't speak as they pass by.
Grand opening to-night of the Miramar
Cafe and Billiard Parlors, cor. Geary and
Leavenworth streets, under the manage
ment of E. Himmel and Frank J. Loskay,
as a first-class billiard parlor and club
room. Everybody welcome. ...*-.

INVESTOGATION
OF FRAGLEY IS
INAUGURATED
Supervisors Examine
Witnesses.
The investigation into the alleged mis
conduct of Superintendent of Streets Mar
tin Fragley was inaugurated by the mem
bers of the Finance and Street Commit
tees of the Board of Supervisors yester
day afternoon. Nearly two hours were
devoted to the examination, and although
few questions were propounded to each
man called in, it is thought that the la
bors of the committees have only begun,
as there still remain 200 more witnesses
to examine.
Mr. Fragley, accompanied by his chief
deputy, A. J. Donovan, and his attorney,
John B. Gartland, entered the committee
room shortly after the session had begun.
Supervisor Perrault, chairman of the
committee, propounded but a half dozen
questions to each witness. They we're:
"Where do you work* "What is your
salary?" "How many days did you labor
last month?" "Where did you cash your
warrant?" and as they invariably an
swered "with a broker," they were asked
what commission they paid him. -i;
W. T. Sullivan, father of Mayor Phe
lan's secretary, testified that he was
earning $62 50 and had put that amount in
his pocket, excepting the amount he paid
a broker. Chairman Perrault decided -not
to ask the witness any more questions
out of respect to the co.onel. and the old
gentleman was allowed to deport.
As the trend of examination became ap
parent to Mr. Fragley and his attorney
they sat. back and took things easy. A
smile covered the Superintendent's coun
tenance and he was seemingly at peace
with the world. Martin Fragley Jr. was
called in to testify, but the cnairman al
lowed him to depart without interrogat
ing him. , . , ...
When J Kelly was examined he testi
fied thai he received $63 50, and as the
warrant called for $70 it looked as if some
wrongdoing was discovered. The witness
removed all suspicion by stating that it
must be another -Kelly, as - there were
two of the same name in the department.
Supervisor Attridge renewed his motion
to adjourn, but he was prevailed upon
to. withdraw it. A dozen more men were
examined, but all the inquisitors learned
was the name of the broker who charged
the least percentage. An adjournment
was taken until further notice from
Chairman Perrault. 'YY
It was learned after the meeting that
since the McGlade trial the Supervisors
have been desirous to discover whether
there are any "dummies" drawing pay
from the Street Department. The only
way to ascertain whether there are is to
subpena every man whose warrant is in
the hands of the board.
The Dog Fighters' Pull.
The cases against fifteen men accused
of preparing to engage in a dog fight in
of preparing to engage in a dog fight in
a pit in a saloon at the corner of Six
teenth and Church streets were called in
acting Police Judge Groezinger's court
yesterday and were stricken from the cal
endar, the Judge fining each $10, with no
alternative. . ,
Queer Cure for Vagrancy.
Ignacio Coronel was arrested Thursday
on the charge of vagrancy. He lives at
536 Vallejo street' and spent his time in
hanging around saloons on the Bnrbary
Coast. When the case was called In
Judge Graham's court yesterday his
mother and Librada Morales, a young
girl, appeared and pleaded for him. The
girl said they were engaged to be mar
ried, and as Coronel expressed his willing
ness to get married and lead a better life
the marriage license* was procured and
Justice of the Peace Kerrigan tied the
knot. Judge Graham then dismissed the
charge of vagrancy.

Handball Entries for Sunday
The entries for Sunday's handball games
at Phil Ryan's court. 858 Howard street,
have been announced. In addition to the
schedule of regular entries a match for
Phil Ryan's trophy will be contested for
by E. Foy and M. McClure against M.
Maguire and E. Curley with the best three
out of five games.
The entries for the day are:

and M. McDonald.

San Francisco Club, and M. McCltlre, welter
weight of the same club, vs. M. Maguire and E.
Curley, three games in five to win.

The Blackmailing Soldier.
The case of Guy C. Weid, the dis
charged soldier who was arrested for
stealing papers from Major Matthews at
the Presidio with the object of black
mailing him. was called in Judge Mogan's
court yesterday, but was continued till
May 24, owing to the illness of the prin
cipal witness. Sergeant Baldwin, who ar
rested Weid. states that he also attempt
ed to blackmail A. R. Exley, an insurance
man of Oakland.
